## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Scheduler Framework Plugin Extension Points

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that define the scheduler framework plugin extension points: the PreFilter, Filter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, and PostBind interfaces and their registration in the scheduler framework.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

322026-03-08T21:58:20.533045agentmessage-
The answer.json file has been created and validated. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

### Core Interface File
**`pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go`** is the single canonical source defining all scheduler framework plugin extension point interfaces:
- `PreFilterPlugin` (line 512) — called at the start of the scheduling cycle
- `FilterPlugin` (line 540) — filters nodes that cannot run the pod
- `PreScorePlugin` (line 587) — informational, called after filtering
- `ScorePlugin` (line 607) — ranks filtered nodes
- `ReservePlugin` (line 624) — updates state when a node is assigned
- `PermitPlugin` (line 660) — can prevent or delay pod binding
- `PreBindPlugin` (line 640) — called before binding
- `BindPlugin` (line 673) — binds the pod to a node
- `PostBindPlugin` (line 649) — called after successful binding

### Framework Runtime (Registration)
- **`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go`** — `frameworkImpl` holds plugin slices per extension point; `getExtensionPoints()` maps config to slices; `NewFramework()` initializes and registers plugins
- **`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go`** — `Registry` type and `PluginFactory` for plugin instantiation
- **`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/instrumented_plugins.go`** — metric-instrumented wrappers for Filter, PreFilter, PreScore, Score
- **`pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go`** — `NewInTreeRegistry()` registers all built-in plugins

### Plugin Implementations
All in-tree plugins implementing these interfaces are in `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/` subdirectories (interpodaffinity, volumebinding, nodeaffinity, podtopologyspread, tainttoleration, noderesources, nodeports, nodename, nodeunschedulable, nodevolumelimits, volumerestrictions, volumezone, imagelocality, dynamicresources, defaultbi

\\\\treturn \\\\u0026PodsToActivate{Map: make(map[string]*v1.Pod)}\\\\n286: }\\\\n287: \\\\n288: // Status indicates the result of running a plugin. // LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\\\\n459: type LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 *QueuedPodInfo) bool\\\\n460: \\\\n461: // QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\\\\\"QueueSort\\\\\\\" plugins.\\\\n462: // These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\\\\n463: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\\\\n464: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\\\\n465: \\\\tPlugin\\\\n466: \\\\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\\\\n467: \\\\tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\\\\n468: }\\\\n469: \\\\n470: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\\\\n471: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\\\\n472: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\\\\n473: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\\\\n474: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\\\\n475: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\\\\n476: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\\\\n477: // and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\\\\n478: //\\\\n479: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\\\\n480: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\\\\n481: // And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\\\\n482: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\\\\n483: \\\\tPlugin\\\\n484: \\\\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\\\\n485: \\\\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\\\\n486: \\\\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\\\n487: \\\\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\\\\n488: \\\\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\\\\n489: \\\\t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\\\\n490: \\\\t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\\\\n491: \\\\t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\\\\n492: \\\\t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\\\\n493: \\\\t//\\\\n494: \\\\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\\\\n495: \\\\tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\\\\n496: }\\\\n497: \\\\n498: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\\\\n499: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\\\\n500: // state.\\\\n501: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\\\\n502: \\\\t// AddPod is called by the framework while \\\\n510: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\\\\\"PreFilter\\\\\\\" plugins.\\\\n511: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\\\\n512: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\\\\n513: \\\\tPlugin\\\\n514: \\\\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\\\\n515: \\\\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. In\\\\n728: \\\\t// such case, pod will not be scheduled.\\\\n729: \\\\tRunReservePluginsReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\\\n730: \\\\n731: \\\\t// RunReservePluginsUnreserve runs the Unreserve method of the set of\\\\n732: \\\\t// configured Reserve plugins.\\\\n733: \\\\tRunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\\\n734: \\\\n735: \\\\t// RunPermitPlugins runs the set of configured Permit plugins. NodeToStatus contains the statuses of the Nodes where the incoming Pod was not schedulable.\\n68: type NodeToStatus struct {\\n69: \\t// nodeToStatus contains specific statuses of the nodes.\\n70: \\tnodeToStatus map[string]*Status\\n71: \\t// absentNodesStatus defines a status for all nodes that are absent in nodeToStatus map.\\n72: \\t// By default, all absent nodes are }\\n81: \\n82: // NewNodeToStatus creates NodeToStatus initialized with given nodeToStatus and absentNodesStatus.\\n83: func NewNodeToStatus(nodeToStatus map[string]*Status, absentNodesStatus *Status) If the node is not in the map, the absentNodesStatus is returned.\\n91: func (m *NodeToStatus) Get(nodeName string) *Status {\\n92: \\tif status, ok := m.nodeToStatus[nodeName]; ok {\\n93: \\t\\treturn status\\n94: \\t}\\n95: \\treturn m.absentNodesStatus\\n96: }\\n97: \\n98: // Set sets status for given nodeName.\\n99: func (m *NodeToStatus) Set(nodeName string, status *Status) {\\n100: \\tm.nodeToStatus[nodeName] = status\\n101: }\\n102: \\n103: // Len returns length of nodeToStatus map. *NodeToStatus) SetAbsentNodesStatus(status *Status) {\\n115: \\tm.absentNodesStatus = status\\n116: }\\n117: \\n118: // ForEachExplicitNode runs fn for each node which status is explicitly set.\\n119: // Imporatant note, it runs the fn only for nodes with a status explicitly registered,\\n120: // and hence may not run the fn for all existing nodes.\\n121: // For example, if PreFilter rejects all Nodes, the scheduler would NOT set a failure status to every Node,\\n122: // but set a failure status as AbsentNodesStatus.\\n123: // You're supposed to get a status from AbsentNodesStatus(), and consider all other nodes that are rejected by them.\\n124: func (m *NodeToStatus) ForEachExplicitNode(fn func(nodeName string, status *Status)) {\\n125: \\tfor nodeName, status := range m.nodeToStatus {\\n126: \\t\\tfn(nodeName, status)\\n127: \\t}\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: // NodesForStatusCode returns a list of NodeInfos for the nodes that matches a given status code.\\n131: // If the absentNodesStatus matches the code, all existing nodes are fetched using nodeLister\\n132: // and filtered using NodeToStatus.Get.\\n133: // If the absentNodesStatus doesn't match the code, nodeToStatus map is used to create a list of nodes\\n134: // and nodeLister.Get is used to obtain NodeInfo for each.\\n135: func (m *NodeToStatus) NodesForStatusCode(nodeLister NodeInfoLister, code Code) ([]*NodeInfo, error) {\\n136: \\tvar resultNodes []*NodeInfo\\n137: \\n138: \\tif m.AbsentNodesStatus().Code() == code {\\n139: \\t\\tallNodes, err := nodeLister.List()\\n140: \\t\\tif err != nil {\\n141: \\t\\t\\treturn nil, err\\n142: \\t\\t}\\n143: \\t\\tif m.Len() == 0 {\\n144: \\t\\t\\t// All nodes are absent and status code is matching, so can return all nodes.\\n145: \\t\\t\\treturn allNodes, nil\\n146: \\t\\t}\\n147: \\t\\t// Need to find all the nodes that are absent or have a matching code using the allNodes.\\n148: \\t\\tfor _, node := range allNodes {\\n149: \\t\\t\\tnodeName := node.Node().Name\\n150: \\t\\t\\tif status := m.Get(nodeName); status.Code() == code {\\n151: \\t\\t\\t\\tresultNodes = append(resultNodes, node)\\n152: \\t\\t\\t}\\n153: \\t\\t}\\n154: \\t\\treturn resultNodes, nil\\n155: \\t}\\n156: \\n157: \\tm.ForEachExplicitNode(func(nodeName string, status *Status) {\\n158: \\t\\tif status.Code() == code {\\n159: \\t\\t\\tif nodeInfo, err := nodeLister.Get(nodeName); err == nil {\\n160: \\t\\t\\t\\tresultNodes = append(resultNodes, nodeInfo)\\n161: \\t\\t\\t}\\n162: \\t\\t}\\n163: \\t})\\n164: \\n165: \\treturn resultNodes, nil\\n166: }\\n167: \\n168: // NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\\n169: type NodePluginScores struct {\\n170: \\t// Name is node name.\\n171: \\tName string\\n172: \\t// Scores is scores from plugins and extenders.\\n173: \\tScores []PluginScore\\n174: \\t// TotalScore is the total score in Scores.\\n175: \\tTotalScore int64\\n176: }\\n177: \\n178: // PluginScore is a struct with plugin/extender name and score.\\n179: type PluginScore struct {\\n180: \\t// Name is the name of plugin or extender.\\n181: \\tName  string\\n182: \\tScore int64\\n183: }\\n184: \\n185: // Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\\n186: type Code int\\n187: \\n188: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\\n189: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\\n190: const (\\n191: \\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\\n192: \\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \\\"Success\\\".\\n193: \\tSuccess Code = iota\\n194: \\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\\n195: \\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\\n196: \\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\\n197: \\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\\n198: \\tError\\n199: \\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\\n200: \\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\\n201: \\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\\n202: \\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\\n203: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n204: \\t//\\n205: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n206: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\\n207: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n208: \\tUnschedulable\\n209: \\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\\n210: \\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\\n211: \\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\\n212: \\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\\n213: \\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\\n214: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n215: \\t//\\n216: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n217: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n218: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n219: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n220: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n221: \\tWait\\n222: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n223: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n224: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n225: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n226: \\tSkip\\n227: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n228: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n229: \\t//\\n230: \\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\\n231: \\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\\n232: \\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\\n233: \\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\\n234: \\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\\n235: \\t//\\n236: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n237: \\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\\n238: \\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\\n239: \\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\\n240: \\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\\n241: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\\n242: \\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\\n243: \\tPending\\n244: )\\n245: \\n246: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\\n247: var codes = []string{\\\"Success\\\", \\\"Error\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\", \\\"Wait\\\", \\\"Skip\\\", \\\"Pending\\\"}\\n248: \\n249: func (c Code) String() string {\\n250: \\treturn codes[c]\\n251: }\\n252: \\n253: const (\\n254: \\t//
